<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>The Lord of the Rings</i> (film series)</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="hatnote">This article is about the film series released in 2001 to 2003. <p><i><b>The Lord of the Rings</b></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Film_series" title="Film series">film series</a> consisting of three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epic_fantasy" title="Epic fantasy">epic fantasy</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adventure_films" title="Adventure films">adventure films</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a>. They are based on the novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a>. The films are subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">The Fellowship of the Ring</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">The Two Towers</a></i> (2002) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i> (2003). They were distributed by <a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">New Line Cinema</a>.</p>
<p>Considered to be one of the biggest and most ambitious film projects ever undertaken, with an overall budget of $281 million (some sources say $310 million-$330 million),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> the entire project took eight years, with the filming for all three films done simultaneously and entirely in New Zealand, Jackson's native country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Each film in the series also had special extended editions released on DVD a year after their respective theatrical releases. While the films follow the book's general storyline, they do omit some of the novel's plot elements and include some additions to and deviations from the source material.</p>
<p>Set in the fictional world of <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a>, the films follow the <a href="/wiki/Hobbit" title="Hobbit">hobbit</a> <a href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins" title="Frodo Baggins">Frodo Baggins</a> (<a href="/wiki/Elijah_Wood" title="Elijah Wood">Elijah Wood</a>) as he and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring_(characters)" title="The Fellowship of the Ring (characters)">Fellowship</a> embark on a quest to destroy the <a href="/wiki/One_Ring" title="One Ring">One Ring</a>, and thus ensure the destruction of its maker, the Dark Lord <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">Sauron</a>. The Fellowship becomes divided and Frodo continues the quest together with his loyal companion <a href="/wiki/Samwise_Gamgee" title="Samwise Gamgee">Sam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sean_Astin" title="Sean Astin">Sean Astin</a>) and the treacherous <a href="/wiki/Gollum" title="Gollum">Gollum</a> (<a href="/wiki/Andy_Serkis" title="Andy Serkis">Andy Serkis</a>). Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a> (<a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a>), heir in exile to the throne of <a href="/wiki/Gondor" title="Gondor">Gondor</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(Middle-earth)" title="Wizard (Middle-earth)">wizard</a> <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">Gandalf</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a>) unite and rally the <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth_peoples#Free_peoples" title="Middle-earth peoples">Free Peoples of Middle-earth</a> in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Ring" title="War of the Ring">War of the Ring</a>.</p>
<p>The series was a major financial success, with the films collectively being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_franchises_and_film_series" title="List of highest-grossing franchises and film series">among the highest-grossing film series</a> of all time. The films were critically acclaimed and <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="List of accolades received by The Lord of the Rings film series">heavily awarded</a>, winning 17 out of 30 total <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominations. The final film in the series, <i>The Return of the King</i>, won all of its 11 Academy Awards nominations, tying it with <i><a href="/wiki/Ben-Hur_(1959_film)" title="Ben-Hur (1959 film)">Ben-Hur</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> for most Academy Awards received for a film. The series received wide praise for its innovative special and visual effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Director Peter Jackson first came into contact with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> when he saw <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bakshi" title="Ralph Bakshi">Ralph Bakshi</a>'s 1978 animated film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1978_film)" title="The Lord of the Rings (1978 film)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>. Jackson "enjoyed the film and wanted to know more."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Afterwards, he read a tie-in edition of the book<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> during a twelve-hour train journey from <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a> to <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> when he was seventeen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sibley-11_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sibley-11-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1995, Jackson was finishing <i><a href="/wiki/The_Frighteners" title="The Frighteners">The Frighteners</a></i> and considered <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> as a new project, wondering "why nobody else seemed to be doing anything about it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sibley-11_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sibley-11-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> With the new developments in <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> following <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_(film)" title="Jurassic Park (film)">Jurassic Park</a></i>, Jackson set about planning a fantasy film that would be relatively serious and feel real. By October, he and his partner <a href="/wiki/Fran_Walsh" title="Fran Walsh">Fran Walsh</a> teamed up with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miramax_Films" title="Miramax Films">Miramax Films</a> boss <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Weinstein" title="Harvey Weinstein">Harvey Weinstein</a> to negotiate with <a href="/wiki/Saul_Zaentz" title="Saul Zaentz">Saul Zaentz</a> who had held the <a href="/wiki/Film_rights" title="Film rights">rights</a> to the book since the early 1970s, pitching an adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i> and two films based on <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>. Negotiations then stalled when <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a> offered Jackson a <a href="/wiki/Remake" title="Remake">remake</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(1933_film)" title="King Kong (1933 film)">King Kong</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cheat_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-cheat-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Weinstein was furious, and further problems arose when it turned out Zaentz did not have distribution rights to <i>The Hobbit</i>; <a href="/wiki/United_Artists" title="United Artists">United Artists</a>, which was in the market, did. By April 1996, the rights question was still not resolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cheat_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-cheat-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jackson decided to move ahead with <i>King Kong</i> before filming <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, prompting Universal to enter a deal with Miramax to receive foreign earnings from <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> while Miramax received foreign earnings from <i>King Kong</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cheat_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-cheat-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also revealed that Jackson originally wanted to finish <i>King Kong</i> before <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> began. But due to location problems, he decided to start with <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> franchise instead.</p>
<p>When Universal cancelled <i><a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(2005_film)" title="King Kong (2005 film)">King Kong</a></i> in 1997,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timeline_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Jackson and Walsh immediately received support from Weinstein and began a six-week <a href="/wiki/Chain_of_title" title="Chain of title">process of sorting out the rights</a>. Jackson and Walsh asked <a href="/wiki/Costa_Botes" title="Costa Botes">Costa Botes</a> to write a <a href="/wiki/Abridgement" title="Abridgement">synopsis</a> of the book and they began to re-read the book. Two to three months later, they had written their <a href="/wiki/Film_treatment" title="Film treatment">treatment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quest_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The first film would have dealt with what would become <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">The Fellowship of the Ring</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">The Two Towers</a></i>, and the beginning of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i>, ending with <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">Saruman</a>'s death, and <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">Gandalf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peregrin_Took" title="Peregrin Took">Pippin</a> going to <a href="/wiki/Minas_Tirith" title="Minas Tirith">Minas Tirith</a>. In this treatment, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gwaihir" title="Gwaihir">Gwaihir</a> and Gandalf visit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edoras" title="Edoras">Edoras</a> after escaping Saruman, Gollum attacks Frodo when the Fellowship is still united, and <a href="/wiki/Farmer_Maggot" title="Farmer Maggot">Farmer Maggot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glorfindel" title="Glorfindel">Glorfindel</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radagast_(Middle-earth)" title="Radagast (Middle-earth)">Radagast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elladan_and_Elrohir" title="Elladan and Elrohir">Elladan and Elrohir</a> are present. Bilbo attends the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Elrond" title="Council of Elrond">Council of Elrond</a>, Sam looks into <a href="/wiki/Galadriel" title="Galadriel">Galadriel</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mirror_of_Galadriel" title="Mirror of Galadriel">mirror</a>, Saruman is redeemed before he dies and the <a href="/wiki/Nazg%C3%BBl" title="NazgÃ»l">NazgÃ»l</a> just make it into <a href="/wiki/Mount_Doom" title="Mount Doom">Mount Doom</a> before they fall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quest_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> They presented their treatment to Harvey and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Weinstein" title="Bob Weinstein">Bob Weinstein</a>, the latter of whom they focused on impressing with their screenwriting as he had not read the book. They agreed upon two films and a total budget of $75Â million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quest_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During mid-1997,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Jackson and Walsh began writing with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sinclair" title="Stephen Sinclair">Stephen Sinclair</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quest_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Sinclair's partner, <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Boyens" title="Philippa Boyens">Philippa Boyens</a>, was a major fan of the book and joined the writing team after reading their treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> It took 13â14 months to write the two film scripts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> which were 147 and 144 pages respectively. Sinclair left the project due to theatrical obligations. Amongst their revisions, Sam is caught eavesdropping and forced to go along with Frodo, instead of Sam, Merry, and Pippin figuring out about the One Ring themselves and voluntarily going along after confronting Frodo about it, as occurs in the original novel. Gandalf's account of his time at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthanc" title="Orthanc">Orthanc</a> was pulled out of flashback and <a href="/wiki/Lothl%C3%B3rien" title="LothlÃ³rien">LothlÃ³rien</a> was cut, with Galadriel doing what she does in the story at Rivendell. <a href="/wiki/Denethor" title="Denethor">Denethor</a> attends the Council with his son. Other changes included having <a href="/wiki/Arwen" title="Arwen">Arwen</a> rescue Frodo, and the action sequence involving the cave <a href="/wiki/Troll_(Middle-earth)" title="Troll (Middle-earth)">troll</a>. Arwen was even going to kill the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Witch-king" title="Witch-king">Witch-king</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quest_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Trouble struck when <a href="/wiki/Marty_Katz" title="Marty Katz">Marty Katz</a> was sent to New Zealand. Spending four months there, he told Miramax that the films were more likely to cost $150Â million, and with Miramax unable to finance this, and with $15Â million already spent, they decided to merge the two films into one. On 17 June 1998, Bob Weinstein presented a treatment of a single two-hour film version of the book. He suggested cutting <a href="/wiki/Bree_(Middle-earth)" title="Bree (Middle-earth)">Bree</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Helm%27s_Deep" title="Battle of Helm's Deep">Battle of Helm's Deep</a>, "losing or using" <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">Saruman</a>, merging <a href="/wiki/Rohan_(Middle-earth)" title="Rohan (Middle-earth)">Rohan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gondor" title="Gondor">Gondor</a> with <a href="/wiki/%C3%89owyn" title="Ãowyn">Ãowyn</a> as <a href="/wiki/Boromir" title="Boromir">Boromir</a>'s sister, shortening <a href="/wiki/Rivendell" title="Rivendell">Rivendell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)" title="Moria (Middle-earth)">Moria</a> as well as having <a href="/wiki/Ent" title="Ent">Ents</a> prevent the <a href="/wiki/Uruk-hai" title="Uruk-hai">Uruk-hai</a> kidnapping Merry and Pippin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quest_13-5"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Upset by the idea of "cutting out half the good stuff"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Jackson balked, and Miramax declared that any script or work completed by <a href="/wiki/Weta_Workshop" title="Weta Workshop">Weta Workshop</a> was theirs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quest_13-6"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Jackson went around Hollywood for four weeks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> showing a thirty-five-minute video of their work, before meeting with <a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">New Line Cinema</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ordesky" title="Mark Ordesky">Mark Ordesky</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> At New Line Cinema, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Shaye" title="Robert Shaye">Robert Shaye</a> viewed the video, and then asked why they were making two films when the book was published as three volumes (this was later corrected: New Line only made this choice out of economical reasons);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> he wanted to make a film trilogy. Now Jackson, Walsh, and Boyens had to write three new scripts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The expansion to three films allowed much more creative freedom, although Jackson, Walsh, and Boyens had to restructure their script accordingly. The three films do not correspond exactly to the trilogy's three volumes, but rather represent a three-part <a href="/wiki/Film_adaptation" title="Film adaptation">adaptation</a>. Jackson takes a more <a href="/wiki/Chronology" title="Chronology">chronological</a> approach to the story than did Tolkien. Frodo's quest is the main focus, and Aragorn is the main sub-plot,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> and many sequences (such as <a href="/wiki/Tom_Bombadil" title="Tom Bombadil">Tom Bombadil</a>) that do not contribute directly to those two plots were left out. Much effort was put into creating satisfactory conclusions and making sure <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exposition_(literary_technique)" title="Exposition (literary technique)">exposition</a> did not bog down the pacing. Amongst new sequences, there are also expansions on elements Tolkien kept ambiguous, such as the <a href="/wiki/Battle" title="Battle">battles</a> and the creatures. During <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking#Production" title="Filmmaking">shooting</a>, the screenplays continued to evolve, in part due to contributions from cast looking to further explore their characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Most notable amongst these rewrites was the character <a href="/wiki/Arwen" title="Arwen">Arwen</a>, who was originally planned as a warrior princess, but reverted to her book counterpart, who remains physically inactive in the story (though she sends moral and military support).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>To develop fight and sword choreography for the series, the filmmakers employed Hollywood sword-master <a href="/wiki/Bob_Anderson_(fencer)" title="Bob Anderson (fencer)">Bob Anderson</a>. Anderson worked directly with the talent including <a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Urban" title="Karl Urban">Karl Urban</a> to develop the film's many sword fights and stunts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Bob Anderson's role in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> series was highlighted in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Reclaiming_the_Blade" title="Reclaiming the Blade">Reclaiming the Blade</a></i>. This documentary on sword martial arts also featured <a href="/wiki/Weta_Workshop" title="Weta Workshop">Weta Workshop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Taylor_(filmmaker)" title="Richard Taylor (filmmaker)">Richard Taylor</a>, <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> illustrator John Howe and actors <a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Urban" title="Karl Urban">Karl Urban</a>. All discussed their roles and work on the series as related to the sword.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_design">Production design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Production design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alan_Lee_2005.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="885" data-file-width="577" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Alan_Lee_2005.JPG/170px-Alan_Lee_2005.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Alan_Lee_2005.JPG/255px-Alan_Lee_2005.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Alan_Lee_2005.JPG/340px-Alan_Lee_2005.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alan_Lee_2005.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alan Lee at Worldcon 2005 in Glasgow, August 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Production_design_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="Production design of The Lord of the Rings film series">Production design of The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p>Jackson began <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Storyboarding" title="Storyboarding">storyboarding</a> the series with <a href="/wiki/Christian_Rivers" title="Christian Rivers">Christian Rivers</a> in August 1997 and assigned his crew to begin designing Middle-earth at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTT_Art_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_Art-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Jackson hired long-time collaborator <a href="/wiki/Richard_Taylor_(filmmaker)" title="Richard Taylor (filmmaker)">Richard Taylor</a> to lead <a href="/wiki/Weta_Workshop" title="Weta Workshop">Weta Workshop</a> on five major design elements: armour, weapons, prosthetics/make-up, creatures, and miniatures. In November 1997,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> famed Tolkien illustrators <a href="/wiki/Alan_Lee_(illustrator)" title="Alan Lee (illustrator)">Alan Lee</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Howe_(illustrator)" title="John Howe (illustrator)">John Howe</a> joined the project. Most of the imagery in the films is based on their various illustrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lord_of_the_Films_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lord_of_the_Films-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Production_designer" title="Production designer">Production designer</a> <a href="/wiki/Grant_Major" title="Grant Major">Grant Major</a> was charged with the task of converting Lee and Howe's designs into architecture, creating models of the sets, while <a href="/wiki/Dan_Hennah" title="Dan Hennah">Dan Hennah</a> worked as <a href="/wiki/Art_director#In_film" title="Art director">art director</a>, scouting locations and organising the building of sets.</p>
<p>Jackson's vision of <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a> was described as being "<a href="/wiki/Ray_Harryhausen" title="Ray Harryhausen">Ray Harryhausen</a> meets <a href="/wiki/David_Lean" title="David Lean">David Lean</a>" by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Randy_Cook" title="Randy Cook">Randy Cook</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Jackson wanted a gritty realism and historical regard for the fantasy, and attempted to make the world rational and believable. For example, the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Army" title="New Zealand Army">New Zealand Army</a> helped build <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hobbiton" title="Hobbiton">Hobbiton</a> months before filming began so the plants could really grow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Creatures were designed to be biologically believable, such as the enormous wings of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fell_beast_(Middle-earth)" title="Fell beast (Middle-earth)">fell beast</a> to help it fly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> In total, 48,000 pieces of armour, 500 bows, and 10,000 arrows were created by Weta Workshop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilogy_book_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trilogy_book-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> They also created many prosthetics, such as 1,800 pairs of Hobbit feet for the lead actors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-8"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as many ears, noses, and heads for the cast, and around 19,000 costumes were woven and aged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-9"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Every prop was specially designed by the Art Department, taking the different scales into account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-10"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="Principal photography of The Lord of the Rings film series">Principal photography of The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casco_de_Rohirrim.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Casco_de_Rohirrim.jpg/200px-Casco_de_Rohirrim.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Casco_de_Rohirrim.jpg/300px-Casco_de_Rohirrim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Casco_de_Rohirrim.jpg/400px-Casco_de_Rohirrim.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Casco_de_Rohirrim.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A helmet of the Rohirrim.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> for all three films was conducted concurrently in many locations within New Zealand's conservation areas and national parks between 11 October 1999, and 22 December 2000, a period of 438 days. <a href="/wiki/Pick-up_(filmmaking)" title="Pick-up (filmmaking)">Pick-up</a> shoots were conducted annually from 2001 to 2004. The series was shot at over 150 different locations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilogy_book_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Trilogy_book-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> with seven different units shooting, as well as soundstages around <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queenstown,_New_Zealand" title="Queenstown, New Zealand">Queenstown</a>. As well as Jackson directing the whole production, other unit directors included John Mahaffie, <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Murphy" title="Geoff Murphy">Geoff Murphy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fran_Walsh" title="Fran Walsh">Fran Walsh</a>, Barrie Osbourne, Rick Porras, and any other assistant director, producer, or writer available. Jackson monitored these units with live satellite feeds, and with the added pressure of constant script re-writes and the multiple units interpreting his envisioned result, he only got around four hours of sleep a night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to the remoteness of some of the locations, the crew would also bring survival kits in case helicopters could not reach the location to bring them home in time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-11"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Department_of_Conservation" title="New Zealand Department of Conservation">New Zealand Department of Conservation</a> was criticised for approving the filming within national parks without adequate consideration of the adverse environmental effects and without public notification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The adverse effects of filming battle scenes in <a href="/wiki/Tongariro_National_Park" title="Tongariro National Park">Tongariro National Park</a> meant that the park later required restoration work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-production">Post-production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Post-production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg/200px-Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg/300px-Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg/400px-Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An example of Elvish armour from the films.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Each film had the benefit of a full year of post-production time before its respective December release, often finishing in OctoberâNovember, with the crew immediately going to work on the next film. In this period's later part, Jackson would move to London to supervise the scoring and continue editing, while having a computer feed for discussions to The Dorchester Hotel, and a "fat pipe" of Internet connections from <a href="/wiki/Pinewood_Studios" title="Pinewood Studios">Pinewood Studios</a> to look at the special effects. He had a <a href="/wiki/Polycom" title="Polycom">Polycom</a> video link and <a href="/wiki/5.1_surround_sound" title="5.1 surround sound">5.1 surround sound</a> to organise meetings, and listen to new music and sound effects generally wherever he was. The extended editions also had a tight schedule at the start of each year to complete special effects and music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Editing">Editing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Editing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To avoid pressure, Jackson hired a different editor for each film. <a href="/wiki/John_Gilbert_(film_editor)" title="John Gilbert (film editor)">John Gilbert</a> worked on the first film, <a href="/wiki/Michael_J._Horton" title="Michael J. Horton">Mike Horton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jabez_Olssen" title="Jabez Olssen">Jabez Olssen</a> on the second and longtime Jackson collaborator <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Selkirk" title="Jamie Selkirk">Jamie Selkirk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Annie_Collins" title="Annie Collins">Annie Collins</a> on the third. Daily rushes would often last up to four hours, with scenes being done throughout 1999â2002 for the rough (4Â½ hours) assemblies of the films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-12"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> In total, 1828 km (six million feet) of film<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilogy_book_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Trilogy_book-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> was edited down to the 11 hours and 23Â minutes (683Â minutes) of Extended running time. This was the final area of shaping of the films, when Jackson realised that sometimes the best scripting could be redundant on screen, as he picked apart scenes every day from multiple takes.</p>
<p>The first film's editing was relatively easygoing, with Jackson coming up with the concept of an Extended Edition later on, although after a screening to New Line they had to re-edit the beginning for a prologue. <i>The Two Towers</i> was always acknowledged by the crew as the most difficult film to make, as "it had no beginning or end", and had the additional problem of inter-cutting storylines appropriately. Jackson even continued editing the film when that part of the schedule officially ended, resulting in some scenes, including the reforging of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/And%C3%BAril" title="AndÃºril">AndÃºril</a>, Gollum's back-story, and Saruman's demise, being moved to <i>The Return of the King</i>. Later, Saruman's demise was cut from the theatrical edition (but included in the Extended edition) when Jackson felt it was not starting the third film effectively enough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> As with all parts of the third film's post-production, editing was very chaotic. The first time Jackson actually saw the completed film was at the Wellington premiere.</p>
<p>Many filmed scenes remain unused, even in the Extended Editions. Promotional material for <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> contained an attack by <a href="/wiki/Orc_(Middle-earth)" title="Orc (Middle-earth)">Orcs</a> from Moria on LothlÃ³rien after the Fellowship leaves Moria, replaced with a more suspenseful entrance for the Fellowship. Also cut were scenes from the book, including Frodo seeing more of Middle-earth at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parth_Galen" title="Parth Galen">Parth Galen</a> and an extended Council of Elrond,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-13"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> and new scenes with an attack upon Frodo and Sam at the river <a href="/wiki/Anduin" title="Anduin">Anduin</a> by an Uruk-hai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-14"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The major cut to <i>The Two Towers</i> featured Arwen and Elrond visiting Galadriel at LothlÃ³rien, with Arwen then leading the Elven reinforcements to Helm's Deep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> This scene, and a flashback to Arwen and Aragorn's first meeting, was cut during a revision of the film's plot; the Elves' appearance was explained with a telepathic communication between Elrond and Galadriel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ãowyn was to have a greater role in defending the refugees in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glittering_Caves" title="Glittering Caves">Glittering Caves</a> from Uruk-hai intruders,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> while in Osgiliath, Faramir was to have a vision of Frodo becoming like Gollum,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> with Frodo and Sam having an extended fight sequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Filmed for <i>The Return of the King</i> were two scenes present in the book; Sam using the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_objects" title="List of Middle-earth objects">Phial of Galadriel</a> to pass the Watchers at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cirith_Ungol" title="Cirith Ungol">Cirith Ungol</a>, and further epilogue footage, with endings for Legolas and Gimli, Ãowyn and Faramir's wedding and Aragorn's death and funeral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Sauron was to fight Aragorn at the Black Gate, but with Jackson deciding the scene was inappropriate, a computer-generated Troll was used instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> To give context for Wormtongue killing Saruman, and Legolas in turn killing Wormtongue, it was to be revealed Wormtongue poisoned <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9odred" title="ThÃ©odred">ThÃ©odred</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The final scene cut was Aragorn having his armour fitted for the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Morannon" title="Battle of the Morannon">Battle of the Black Gate</a> by the trilogy's armourers, which was the final scene filmed during principal photography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Peter Jackson has stated that he would like to include some of these unused scenes in a future "Ultimate Edition" home video release, also including out-takes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="Music of The Lord of the Rings film series">Music of The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Howard_Shore" title="Howard Shore">Howard Shore</a> composed, orchestrated, conducted, and produced the trilogy's music. He was hired in August 2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> and visited the set, and watched the assembly cuts of <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> and <i>The Return of the King</i>. In the music, Shore included many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leitmotifs" title="Leitmotifs">leitmotifs</a> to represent various characters, cultures, and places. For example, there are leitmotifs for the hobbits as well as the <a href="/wiki/Shire_(Middle-earth)" title="Shire (Middle-earth)">Shire</a>. Although the first film had some of its score recorded in Wellington,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_14-15"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> virtually all of the trilogy's score was recorded in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watford_Colosseum" title="Watford Colosseum">Watford Town Hall</a> and mixed at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a>. Jackson planned to advise the score for six weeks each year in London, though for <i>The Two Towers</i> he stayed for twelve. As a <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">Beatles</a> fan, Jackson had a photo tribute done there on the <a href="/wiki/Zebra_crossing" title="Zebra crossing">zebra crossing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_18-5"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The score is primarily played by the <a href="/wiki/London_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="London Philharmonic Orchestra">London Philharmonic Orchestra</a>, and many artists such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Del_Maestro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ben Del Maestro (page does not exist)">Ben Del Maestro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enya" title="Enya">Enya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9e_Fleming" title="RenÃ©e Fleming">RenÃ©e Fleming</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Galway" title="James Galway">James Galway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emil%C3%ADana_Torrini" title="EmilÃ­ana Torrini">EmilÃ­ana Torrini</a> contributed. Even actors <a href="/wiki/Billy_Boyd_(actor)" title="Billy Boyd (actor)">Billy Boyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liv_Tyler" title="Liv Tyler">Liv Tyler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miranda_Otto" title="Miranda Otto">Miranda Otto</a> (extended cuts only for the latter two), and Peter Jackson (for a single gong sound in the second film) contributed to the score. Fran Walsh and Philippa Boyens also wrote the lyrics to various music and songs, which <a href="/wiki/David_Salo" title="David Salo">David Salo</a> translated into Tolkien's languages. The third film's end song, "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_West_(song)" title="Into the West (song)">Into the West</a>", was a tribute to a young filmmaker Jackson and Walsh befriended named <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Duncan" title="Cameron Duncan">Cameron Duncan</a>, who died of cancer in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Shore composed a main theme for <i>The Fellowship</i> rather than many different character themes, and its strength and weaknesses in volume are depicted at different points in the series. On top of that, individual themes were composed to represent different cultures. Infamously, the amount of music Shore had to write every day for the third film increased dramatically to around seven minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sound">Sound</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sound">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sound technicians spent the early part of the year trying to find the right sounds. Some, such as animal sounds like tigers' and walruses', were bought. Human voices were also used. Fran Walsh contributed to the NazgÃ»l scream and David Farmer the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warg_(Middle-earth)" title="Warg (Middle-earth)">Warg</a> howls. Other sounds were unexpected: The Fell Beast's screech is taken from that of a donkey, and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%BBmakil" title="MÃ»makil">mÃ»makil</a>'</i>s bellow comes from the beginning and end of a lion's roar. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Dubbing_(filmmaking)" title="Dubbing (filmmaking)">ADR</a> was used for most of the dialogue.</p>
<p>The technicians worked with New Zealand locals to get many of the sounds. They re-recorded sounds in abandoned tunnels for an echo-like effect in the <a href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)" title="Moria (Middle-earth)">Moria</a> sequence. 20,000 New Zealand cricket fans provided the sound of the Uruk-hai army in <i>The Two Towers</i>, with Jackson acting as conductor during the innings break of a one day International cricket match between England and New Zealand at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westpac_Stadium" title="Westpac Stadium">Westpac Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> They spent time recording sounds in a graveyard at night, and also had construction workers drop stone blocks for the sounds of boulders firing and landing in <i>The Return of the King</i>. Mixing took place between August and November at "The Film Mix", before Jackson commissioned the building of a new studio in 2003. The building, however, had not yet been fully completed when they started mixing for <i>The Return of the King</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_effects">Special effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Special effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Special_effects_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="Special effects of The Lord of the Rings film series">Special effects of The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p>The first film has around 540 effect shots, the second 799, and the third 1,488 (2,730 in total). The total increases to 3,420 with the extended editions. 260 visual effect artists began work on the series, and the number doubled by <i>The Two Towers</i>. The crew, led by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Rygiel" title="Jim Rygiel">Jim Rygiel</a> and Randy Cook, worked long hours, often overnight, to produce special effects within a short space of time. Jackson's active imagination was a driving force. For example, several major shots of Helm's Deep were produced within the last six weeks of post-production of <i>The Two Towers</i>, and the same happened again within the last six weeks on <i>The Return of the King</i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Releases">Releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatrical">Theatrical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Theatrical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The trilogy's online promotional trailer was first released on 27 April 2000, and set a new record for download hits, registering 1.7Â million hits in the first 24 hours of its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The trailer used a selection from the soundtrack for <i><a href="/wiki/Braveheart" title="Braveheart">Braveheart</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shawshank_Redemption" title="The Shawshank Redemption">The Shawshank Redemption</a></i> among other cuts. In 2001, 24Â minutes of footage from the series, primarily the <a href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)" title="Moria (Middle-earth)">Moria</a> sequence, was shown at the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a>, and was very well received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The showing also included an area designed to look like <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilogy_book_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-Trilogy_book-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">The Fellowship of the Ring</a></i> was released 19 December 2001. It grossed $47Â million in its U.S. opening weekend and made around $871Â million worldwide. A preview of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">The Two Towers</a></i> was inserted just before the end credits near the end of the film's theatrical run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> A promotional trailer was later released, containing music re-scored from the film <i><a href="/wiki/Requiem_for_a_Dream" title="Requiem for a Dream">Requiem for a Dream</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Two Towers</i> was released 18 December 2002. It grossed $62Â million in its first U.S. weekend and out-grossed its predecessor, grossing $926Â million worldwide. The promotional trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i> was dÃ©buted exclusively before the New Line Cinema film <i><a href="/wiki/Secondhand_Lions" title="Secondhand Lions">Secondhand Lions</a></i> on 23 September 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Released 17 December 2003, its first U.S. weekend gross was $72Â million, and became the second film (after <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>) to gross over $1Â billion worldwide.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Each film was released on standard two-disc edition DVDs containing previews of the next film. The success of the theatrical cuts brought about four-disc Extended Editions, with new editing, added special effects and music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The extended cuts of the films and the included special features were spread over two discs, and a limited collectors edition was also released. <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> was released on 12 November 2002, containing 30Â minutes more footage, an Alan Lee painting of the Fellowship entering Moria, and the Moria Gate on the back of the sleeve and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argonath" title="Argonath">Argonath</a> styled bookend with the Collector's Edition. <i>The Two Towers</i>, released on 18 November 2003, contains 44Â minutes extra footage, a Lee painting of Gandalf the White's entrance and the Collector's Edition contained a SmÃ©agol statue, with a crueller-looking statue of his Gollum persona available for order during a limited time.</p>
<p><i>The Return of the King</i> was released on 14 December 2004, having 51Â minutes more footage, a Lee painting of the Grey Havens and a model of Minas Tirith for the Collector's Edition, with <a href="/wiki/Minas_Morgul" title="Minas Morgul">Minas Morgul</a> available for order during a limited time. The Special Extended DVD Editions also had in-sleeve maps of the Fellowship's travels. They have also played at cinemas, most notably for a 16 December 2003, marathon screening (dubbed "Trilogy Tuesday") culminating in a late afternoon screening of the third film. Attendees of "Trilogy Tuesday" were given a limited edition keepsake from <a href="/wiki/Sideshow_Collectibles" title="Sideshow Collectibles">Sideshow Collectibles</a> containing one random frame of film from each of the three movies. Both versions were put together in a Limited Edition "<a href="/wiki/Seamless_branching" title="Seamless branching">branching</a>" version, plus a new feature-length documentary by <a href="/wiki/Costa_Botes" title="Costa Botes">Costa Botes</a>. The complete series was released in a six Disc set on 14 November 2006.</p>
<p>Warner Bros. released the trilogy's theatrical versions on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> in a boxed set on 6 April 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> An extended edition Blu-ray box set was made available for pre-order from Amazon.com in March 2011 and was released on 28 June 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Each film's extended Blu-ray version is identical to the extended DVD version; the running time includes an added credit sequence listing the names of "<i>Lord of the Rings</i> fan-club members" who contributed to the project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, brand new Blu-ray steelbook editions of the 5-disc Extended Editions were released. The first of which, <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i>, was released on 12 May 2014. The discs are identical to those found in the previous 5-disc Blu-ray set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_and_critical_response">Public and critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public and critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Unadjusted for inflation, <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> film series is the highest grossing film trilogy worldwide of all time, higher even than other film franchises such as the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars#Original_trilogy" title="Star Wars">original <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Godfather_Trilogy" title="Godfather Trilogy"><i>The Godfather</i> trilogy</a>. The film series grossed a total of $2.92 billion. The film series also tied a record with <i><a href="/wiki/Ben-Hur_(1959_film)" title="Ben-Hur (1959 film)">Ben-Hur</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> for the total number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a> won for a single film with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i> receiving eleven Oscars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of critics have also praised the series, with <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Turan" title="Kenneth Turan">Kenneth Turan</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> writing that "the trilogy will not soon, if ever, find its equal".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Some were critical of the films' pacing and length: "It's a collection of spectacular set pieces without any sense of momentum driving them into one another" according to <i>Philadelphia Weekly</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, the films received approval ratings of 91%, 96%, and 95% respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rotfel_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-rotfel-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rottower_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-rottower-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rotreturn_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-rotreturn-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, based on its ratings for each film 92, 88, 94 respectively,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metafel_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-metafel-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metatower_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-metatower-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metareturn_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-metareturn-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> lists the series as one of two most critically acclaimed trilogies of all time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Every film is placed in the top 100 of the 'Metacritic Best-Reviewed Movies' list.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> polls conducted during the opening weekend, cinema audiences gave the series an average grade of A-, A, A+ respectively on an A+ to F scale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cinemascore_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-cinemascore-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The series appears in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas-Fort_Worth_Film_Critics_Association:_Top_10_Films" title="Dallas-Fort Worth Film Critics Association: Top 10 Films">Dallas-Fort Worth Film Critics Association's Top 10 Films</a>, <i>Time</i> magazine's All-Time 100 Movies, and <a href="/wiki/James_Berardinelli" title="James Berardinelli">James Berardinelli</a>'s Top 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> named the series as the most important films of the past 25 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> put it on its end-of-the-decade, "best-of" list, saying, "Bringing a cherished book to the big screen? No sweat. Peter Jackson's trilogyâor, as we like to call it, our preciousssssâexerted its irresistible pull, on advanced Elvish speakers and neophytes alike."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paste_Magazine" title="Paste Magazine">Paste Magazine</a></i> named it one of the 50 Best Movies of the Decade (2000â2009), ranking it at <abbr title="Number">No.</abbr> 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In another <i>Time</i> magazine list, the series ranks second in "Best Movies of the Decade".<i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></i></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academy_Awards">Academy Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Academy Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="List of accolades received by The Lord of the Rings film series">List of accolades received by The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p>The three films together were nominated for a total of 30 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>, of which they won 17, a record for any movie trilogy (the 3 nominations for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_An_Unexpected_Journey" title="The Hobbit: An Unexpected Journey">The Hobbit: An Unexpected Journey</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_The_Desolation_of_Smaug" title="The Hobbit: The Desolation of Smaug">The Hobbit: The Desolation of Smaug</a></i> brings the series' total to 36 nominations). <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> earned thirteen nominations, the most of any film at the <a href="/wiki/74th_Academy_Awards" title="74th Academy Awards">74th Academy Awards</a>, winning four. <i>The Return of the King</i> won in every category in which it was nominated, setting the current Oscar record for the highest clean sweep, and its 11 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> won ties the record held by <i><a href="/wiki/Ben-Hur_(1959_film)" title="Ben-Hur (1959 film)">Ben-Hur</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (though both of those films had additional nominations that they lost out on). <i>The Return of the King</i> became only the second sequel to win the Oscar for Best Picture (after <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather_Part_II" title="The Godfather Part II">The Godfather Part II</a></i>) and the first and only fantasy film to receive this honor, though this has been widely perceived as an award by proxy for the entire series (the first two films were also nominated for Best Picture).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_Times_McNamara_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_McNamara-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> No actors in any of the three films won Oscars, and <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a> was the only actor in the trilogy to receive a nomination which was for his work in <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_Times_McNamara_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_McNamara-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> â Nominations: 13, Wins: 4</li>
<li><i>The Two Towers</i> â Nominations: 6, Wins: 2</li>
<li><i>The Return of the King</i> â Nominations: 11, Wins: 11</li>
</ul>
