<p>As well as Academy Awards, each film in the series won the <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Dramatic_Presentation" title="Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation">Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Award_for_Best_Movie" title="MTV Movie Award for Best Movie">MTV Movie Award for Best Movie</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Fantasy_Film" title="Saturn Award for Best Fantasy Film">Saturn Award for Best Fantasy Film</a>. The first and third films also won the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Film" title="BAFTA Award for Best Film">BAFTA Award for Best Film</a>. The soundtrack for <i>The Two Towers</i> did not receive a nomination because of a rule prohibiting a soundtrack including music from a previous soundtrack to be eligible for nomination. This rule was overturned in time for <i>The Return of the King</i> to receive the Oscar for Best Music Score. The New York Film Critics Circle awarded <i>The Return of the King</i> its Best Picture Award at the 2003 Awards Ceremony, hosted by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnston_(critic)" title="Andrew Johnston (critic)">Andrew Johnston</a>, chair of the organisation at that time, who called it "a masterful piece of filmmaking."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_to_changes_in_the_films_from_the_book">Reactions to changes in the films from the book</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Reactions to changes in the films from the book">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_characters_in_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="List of original characters in The Lord of the Rings film series">List of original characters in The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p>The film series caused reaction amongst fans and scholars of the book and were seen as changing parts Tolkien felt thematically necessary in terms of characters, themes, events and subtlety. Some fans of the book who disagreed with such changes have released <a href="/wiki/Fan_edit" title="Fan edit">fan edits</a> of the films such as <i>The Lord of the Rings: The Purist Edition</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cimmerian_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-cimmerian-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> which removed many of the changes to bring them closer to the original.</p>
<p>Various changes to characters such as <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">Gandalf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arwen" title="Arwen">Arwen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denethor" title="Denethor">Denethor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faramir" title="Faramir">Faramir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gimli_(Middle-earth)" title="Gimli (Middle-earth)">Gimli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins" title="Frodo Baggins">Frodo</a>, when considered together, were seen by some to alter the tone and themes from those found in the book. Several critics contend that the portrayal of women, especially Arwen, in the films is thematically faithful to (or compatible with) Tolkien's writings despite some differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-akers-jordan_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-akers-jordan-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chance_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-chance-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gaydosik_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-gaydosik-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thum_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-thum-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wayne_G._Hammond" title="Wayne G. Hammond">Wayne G. Hammond</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tolkien_research" title="Tolkien research">Tolkien scholar</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> said of the first two films that he found them to be "travesties as adaptations... faithful only on a basic level of plot" and that many characters had not been depicted faithfully to their appearance in the novel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-croft_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-croft-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kirst_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-kirst-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Other critics have argued that Tolkien's characters were weakened and misinterpreted by their portrayal in the films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-revolutionSF_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-revolutionSF-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timmons_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-timmons-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wiggins_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wiggins-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Changes to events (such as the Elves participating at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Hornburg" title="Battle of the Hornburg">Battle of Helm's Deep</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Faramir taking the hobbits to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Osgiliath" title="Osgiliath">Osgiliath</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forum.barrowdowns.com_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-forum.barrowdowns.com-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> and the deletion of the chapter "<a href="/wiki/The_Scouring_of_the_Shire" title="The Scouring of the Shire">The Scouring of the Shire</a>", are seen as changing Tolkien's themes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forum.barrowdowns.com_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-forum.barrowdowns.com-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Janet_Brennan_Croft" title="Janet Brennan Croft">Janet Brennan Croft</a> criticises the films using Tolkien's own terms "anticipation" and "flattening", which he used in critiquing a <a href="/wiki/Adaptations_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings#Early_efforts" title="Adaptations of The Lord of the Rings">proposed film script</a>. She contrasts Tolkien's subtlety with Jackson's tendency to show "too much too soon".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Croft2_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Croft2-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Supporters of the series assert that it is a worthy interpretation of the book and that most of the changes were necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lord_of_the_Films_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lord_of_the_Films-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Many who worked on the series are fans of the book, including <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Lee" title="Christopher Lee">Christopher Lee</a>, who (alone among the cast) had actually met Tolkien in person,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> and Boyens once noted that no matter what, it is simply their interpretation of the book. Jackson once said that to simply summarise the story on screen would be a mess, and in his own words, "Sure, it's not really The Lord of the Rings ... but it could still be a pretty damn cool movie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Other fans also claim that, despite any changes, the films serve as a tribute to the book, appealing to those who have not yet read it, and even leading some to do so. The Movie Guide for The Encyclopedia of <a href="/wiki/Arda_(Middle-earth)" title="Arda (Middle-earth)">Arda</a> (an online Tolkien encyclopaedia) states that Jackson's films were exceptional since filming the whole story of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> was probably impossible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> This notion is partially supported by a review published in 2005 that otherwise criticised a lack in "faithfulness to Tolkien's spirit and tone."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bratman_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-bratman-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Kellner" title="Douglas Kellner">Douglas Kellner</a> argues that the conservative community spirit of Tolkien's Shire is reflected in Jackson's films as well as the division of the Fellowship into "squabbling races".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="664" data-file-width="1024" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg/300px-Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg/450px-Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg/600px-Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Air_New_Zealand" title="Air New Zealand">Air New Zealand</a> painted this <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320</a> in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> livery to help promote the films.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The release of the films saw a surge of interest in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> and Tolkien's other works, vastly increasing his impact on popular culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-surge_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-surge-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> It was rumoured that the Tolkien family became split on the series, with <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Tolkien" title="Christopher Tolkien">Christopher Tolkien</a> and his son <a href="/wiki/Simon_Tolkien" title="Simon Tolkien">Simon Tolkien</a> feuding over whether or not it was a good idea to adapt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Christopher has since denied these claims saying, "My own position is that <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> is peculiarly unsuitable to transformation into visual dramatic form. The suggestions that have been made that I 'disapprove' of the films, even to the extent of thinking ill of those with whom I may differ, are wholly without foundation." He added that he had never "expressed any such feeling".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, however, he described the films as having "eviscerated" the book, and criticised the resulting "commercialisation" of his father's work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Le_Monde_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Le_Monde-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As a result of the series' success, Peter Jackson has become a player in the film business (sometimes called a <a href="/wiki/Business_magnate" title="Business magnate">mogul</a>) in the mould of <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>, in the process befriending some industry heavyweights like <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Singer" title="Bryan Singer">Bryan Singer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Darabont" title="Frank Darabont">Frank Darabont</a>. Jackson has since founded his own film production company, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wingnut_Films" title="Wingnut Films">Wingnut Films</a>, as well as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wingnut_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wingnut Interactive (page does not exist)">Wingnut Interactive</a>, a video-game company. He was also finally given a chance to remake <i><a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(2005_film)" title="King Kong (2005 film)">King Kong</a></i> in 2005. The film became a critical and box office success, although not as successful as <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> series. Jackson has been called a "favourite son" of New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, Howard Shore toured with <i>The Lord of the Rings Symphony</i>, consisting of two hours of the score. Along with the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)"><i>Harry Potter</i> films</a>, the series has renewed interest in the fantasy film genre. Tourism for New Zealand is up, possibly due to its exposure in the series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> with the country's tourism industry waking up to an audience's familiarity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2002, <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_Motion_Picture_Trilogy:_The_Exhibition" title="The Lord of the Rings Motion Picture Trilogy: The Exhibition">The Lord of the Rings Motion Picture Trilogy: The Exhibition</a> opened at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_New_Zealand_Te_Papa_Tongarewa" title="Museum of New Zealand Te Papa Tongarewa">Te Papa museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, New Zealand. As of 2007, the exhibition has travelled to seven other cities around the world. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(theatre)#Toronto" title="The Lord of the Rings (theatre)">musical adaptation</a> of the book was launched in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, Ontario, Canada, in 2006, but it closed after mostly poor reviews. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(theatre)#London" title="The Lord of the Rings (theatre)">shortened version</a> opened in London, United Kingdom, in the summer of 2007. The success of the films has also spawned the production of video games and many other kinds of merchandise.</p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:376px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">
<p>They eviscerated the book by making it an action movie for young people aged 15 to 25, and it seems that <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)" title="The Hobbit (film series)">The Hobbit</a></i> will be the same kind of film. [...] Tolkien has become a monster, devoured by his own popularity and absorbed by the absurdity of our time. The chasm between the beauty and seriousness of the work, and what it has become, has gone too far for me. Such commercialisation has reduced the aesthetic and philosophical impact of this creation to nothing. There is only one solution for me: turning my head away.</p>
</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">â</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">â</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: right;">â<a href="/wiki/Christopher_Tolkien" title="Christopher Tolkien">Christopher Tolkien</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a>,</i> 9 July 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Le_Monde_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Le_Monde-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>The legacy of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> is also that of court cases over profits from the trilogy. Sixteen cast members (Noel Appleby, Jed Brophy, Mark Ferguson, Ray Henwood, Bruce Hopkins, William Johnson, Nathaniel Lees, Sarah McLeod, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Mune" title="Ian Mune">Ian Mune</a>, Paul Norell, Craig Parker, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Pollock_(New_Zealand_actor)" title="Robert Pollock (New Zealand actor)">Robert Pollock</a>, Martyn Sanderson, Peter Tait and Stephan Ure) sued over the lack of revenue from merchandise bearing their appearance. The case was resolved out of court in 2008. The settlement came too late for Appleby, who died of cancer in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saul_Zaentz" title="Saul Zaentz">Saul Zaentz</a> also filed a lawsuit in 2004 claiming he had not been paid all of his royalties. The next year, Jackson himself sued the studio over profits from the first film, slowing development of the prequels until late 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Tolkien_Trust" title="The Tolkien Trust">The Tolkien Trust</a> filed a lawsuit in February 2008, for violating Tolkien's original deal over the rights that they would earn 7.5% of the gross from any films based on his works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> The Trust sought compensation of $150Â million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> A judge denied them this option, but allowed them to win compensation from the act of the studio ignoring the contract itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> On 8 September 2009, a settlement of this dispute between the Trust and New Line was announced (clearing a potential obstacle to the making of a new film based on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Numerous video games have been released to supplement the film series. The releases include: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers_(video_game)" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers (video game)">The Two Towers</a>,</i> <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(pinball)" title="The Lord of the Rings (pinball)">Pinball</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King_(video_game)" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King (video game)">The Return of the King</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Third_Age" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Third Age">The Third Age</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Third_Age_(GBA)" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Third Age (GBA)"><i>The Third Age</i> (GBA)</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_Tactics" title="The Lord of the Rings: Tactics">Tactics</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Battle_for_Middle-earth" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Battle for Middle-earth">The Battle for Middle-earth</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Battle_for_Middle-earth_II" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Battle for Middle-earth II">The Battle for Middle-earth II</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Battle_for_Middle-earth_II:_The_Rise_of_the_Witch-king" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Battle for Middle-earth II: The Rise of the Witch-king">The Battle for Middle-earth II: The Rise of the Witch-king</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_Conquest" title="The Lord of the Rings: Conquest">Conquest</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_Aragorn%27s_Quest" title="The Lord of the Rings: Aragorn's Quest">Aragorn's Quest</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_War_in_the_North" title="The Lord of the Rings: War in the North">War in the North</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(video_game)" title="Lego The Lord of the Rings (video game)">Lego The Lord of the Rings</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Guardians_of_Middle-earth" title="Guardians of Middle-earth">Guardians of Middle-earth</a></i> and the most recent critically acclaimed game <i><a href="/wiki/Middle-earth:_Shadow_of_Mordor" title="Middle-earth: Shadow of Mordor">Middle-earth: Shadow of Mordor</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prequels">Prequels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Prequels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)" title="The Hobbit (film series)">The Hobbit (film series)</a></div>
<p>Peter Jackson has directed three films based on Tolkien's 1937 novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i>. The first film, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_An_Unexpected_Journey" title="The Hobbit: An Unexpected Journey">The Hobbit: An Unexpected Journey</a></i>, was released on 12 December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-titles_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-titles-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The second film, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_The_Desolation_of_Smaug" title="The Hobbit: The Desolation of Smaug">The Desolation of Smaug</a></i>, was released on 13 December 2013, and the third film, subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies" title="The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies">The Battle of the Five Armies</a></i>, was released on 17 December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Several actors from <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, including <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Serkis" title="Andy Serkis">Andy Serkis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Weaving" title="Hugo Weaving">Hugo Weaving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elijah_Wood" title="Elijah Wood">Elijah Wood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Holm" title="Ian Holm">Ian Holm</a> (as older Bilbo), <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Lee" title="Christopher Lee">Christopher Lee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cate_Blanchett" title="Cate Blanchett">Cate Blanchett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">Orlando Bloom</a> reprised their roles.</p>
